HIPAA COMPLIANT MEDICAL AUTHORIZATION (Authorization to Release Protected Health Care Information)

To: Grace Health 121 Bishop Street Corbin, KY 40701

Dear Medical Records Clerk:

I have retained The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to represent me in matters related to an injury sustained due to a third parties’ negligence, Please forward a copy of any & all records not previously provided to The Whaley Law Firm upon requeat.

Pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR 164,508, the provider listed above is hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC or any of thelr representatives, all medical recorda, including but not limited to: Office Notes, History, Physical, Consultation Notes, Discharge Summaries, Orders, Progress Notes, Laboratory Results, Nurses’ Notes, Emergency Room Records, Operative Reports, In-Patlent Records and films of X-Rays, MRIs, CT Scans, or PET Scans, Pharmacy and Drug Records, Medical Bills and Health Insurance Information, Medicaid/Medicare Records, concerning ANY medical treatment that I have received from you and/or at your facility, as well as ALL such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical record file

T hereby authorize the release of ANY & ALL records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes, which must be requested under separate authorization), Chemical Dependency or HIV.

A photostatic copy hereof shall be as valid as the original.

Thereby authorize a PREE COPY of my medical recards purauant to KRS 422.317 be sent to the extent I have not already requested my one free copy,

The purpose of this authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical and mental condition(s), This authorization expires in three (3) years from the date of the algnature. The aforementioned expiration date haa not passed, as thie matter is on-going, I hereby authorize The Whaley Law Pirm, PSC. to speak to my healthcare providers privately or to take the testimony at deposition and/or trial as may be requested,

T have the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice of revocation to the healthcare provider listed above and ta The Whaley Law Firm, PSC, I understand that there are exceptions to the right to revoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity hag taken action in reliance thereon. Medical Providers may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-Listed patent executes this authorization. The information disclosed pursuant to this authorization may be subject to re-disclosure and no longer protected by the privacy regulations promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)

Pain of the Left Shoulder (Left shoulder pain; Ongoing since fall that occurred 4/26/19; Describes a burning sensation; Pain 6/10-worsens with movement; Anti-inflammatories, ice/heat, wearing a sling provide some improvement.)

HPI

Amy Mills is a 35 y.o. female. Patient is here today for second opinion regarding her left shoulder and neck. On 4/26/2019, she slipped and fell in a bank injuring her shoulder and neck. Since that time, she has had difficulty getting treatment she tells me. Editor: Gilbert, Travis Daniel, DO (Physician) VAGINAL HYSTERECTOMY, TENSION FREE VAGINAL TAPING WITH OBTURATOR Procedure Note

Amy Mills 11/5/2018

Pre-op Diagnosis: Uterine prolapse Urinary stress incontinence

Post-op Diagnosis: Uterine prolapse Urinary stress incontinence

Procedure(s):

Total vaginal hysterectomy with left salpingectomy Retropubic tension-free vaginal tape Cystourethroscopy

Surgeon(s): Gilbert, Travis Daniel, DO

Anesthesia: Choice

Estimated Blood Loss: minimal

Specimens:

Procedure: The patient was taken to the operating room after informed written informed consent was obtained. She was prepped and draped in the usual sterile fashion in the dorsal lithotomy position after general anesthesia was obtained. We first placed in speculums anteriorly and posteriorly and grasped the cervix on each of the midline using a toothed tenaculum. We hydrodissected circumferentially around the cervix and then made a circumferential incision around the cervix. We then dissected anteriorly and posteriorly posteriorly we entered the cul-de-sac sharply and placed a retractor. We then dissected anteriorly to the point where we got into the anterior cul-de-sac. Next we took bites on each side using the Haney clamps, we then cut with scissors and suture ligated with 0 Vicryl. We held the sutures for manipulation later on. Next using the LigaSure device we took serial bites on each side of the uterus doubly cauterizing each pedicle and then cutting using the LigaSure. Once we got up to the fundus and the cornua we doubly cauterized it and delivered the uterus. We were able to easily remove the right fallopian tube at the left fallopian tube was little higher in the pelvis and we were on not able to reach it. We then attached the ipsilateral uterosacral ligaments to the

vaginal cuff angles bilaterally and then closed the remainder of the vaginal cuff using interrupted 2-0 Vicryl stitches in a figure-of-eight fashion.

Next we performed the TVT. We isolated the mid urethra between 2 Allis clamps made a 1 cm incision and dissected out laterally and then retropubically. We then placed the TVT trocar through the incision and guided it retropubically and lateral to the urethra we hugged the pubic bone the entire time as we guided it suprapubically. We brought it out through the skin suprapubically. We did this bilaterally. Next we performed a cystourethroscopy making sure that we had not injured the bladder with the TVT trochars and we did not. We then pulled the mesh through and tensioned it loosely io where we could get a pair of Metzenbaum scissors under it easily. We irrigated it. We then closed this incision using a running locking stitch of 2-0 Vicryl.

DIAGNOSIS: Cervical disc herniation with radiculopathy at C3-4: Sprain to the left shoulder

MEDICAL DECISION MAKING: This 35 yr/o female comes to the office today complaining of neck pain. She states that these symptoms began after a fall on 5/25/19 in which she slipped on a wet floor at a bank. She fell forward against a bench and hit the back of her head and her left shoulder. Immediately afterwards, she began to experience pain on the left side of her neck. She also notes left arm pain extending from the upper arm to the mid forearm, and numbness in the fingers of the left hand, which also began after the fall. She feels that this pain is centered at her elbow. Patient notes weakness in the left arm and hand, especially on writing and typing. She is left handed. Strength in the right arm is normal. She complains of headaches on both the right and left sides of the head. She notes some difficulties with balance. She experienced some bladder incontinence immediately following the injury, but states that bladder function has returned to normal. A cervical MRI scan performed recently shows evidence of small disc bulge at C3-4, slightly distorting the spinal cord at that level. Based on the patient's symptoms and radiology, | recommend a EMG and nerve conduction test be performed on the uppet extremities. This test will be performed by Dr. lyer. | recommend the patient to undergo multiple session of cervical physical therapy, as well as physical therapy to the left shoulder, consisting of heat, massage, ultrasound, and exercise that will be performed 3 times per week for 3 weeks. | will see this patient back in my office after the EMG and physical therapy has been completed.

The patient has the following comorbidities: There are no active problems to display for this patient.

PLAN:

1. Cervical physical therapy along with range of motion exercises to the left shoulder. 2. EMG and nerve conduction test of the upper extremities by Dr. lyer.

3. Return to this office after the above procedures are completed.

Assessment

Description

Acute laryngopharyngitis (JO6.0).

There's no cure for the common cold. Antibiotics are of no use against cold viruses and shouldn't be used unless there's a bacterial infection.

To make yourself as comfortable as possible when you have a cold, try:

Drinking plenty of fluids-Water, juice, clear broth or warm lemon water are good choices. Avoid caffeine and alcohol, which can dehydrate you.

Eating chicken soup-Chicken soup/warm fluids can be soothing and can loosen congestion.

Resting-If possible, stay home from work or school if you have a fever or a bad cough or are drowsy after taking medications.

Adjusting your room's temperature and humidity-Keep your room warm, but not overheated. If the air is dry, a cool-mist humidifier or vaporizer can moisten the air and help ease congestion and coughing. Keep the humidifier clean to prevent the growth of bacterial and molds.

Sooth throat-Saltwater gargle can temporarily relieve sore throat.

Saline Nasal Drops-can help relieve nasal congestion, even in children.

Zpack (#1) use as directed

Delsym (120ml) take 5-10ml every 12 hours as needed for cough

Medrol Dose Pack (#1) use as directed

follow-up visit if not improved. Reason for referral: if not improved.

2. Assessment Other headache syndrome (G44.89). Impression Headaches fairly controlled No changes to current medications Monitor and adjust as needed.. Patient Plan How to alleviate headaches

-Apply ice. Hold a cold cloth or an ice pack to the painful area on your head or neck.

Wrap the ice pack in a towel to protect your skin. -Relaxation exercises. Try relaxation exercises to lower stress.

-Biofeedback. Biofeedback may improve your headaches by helping you to monitor how

your body responds to stress.

-Acupuncture. Acupuncture may improve your headaches and help you relax.

-Take over-the-counter pain relievers. Your doctor may recommend you take nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drugs (NSAIDs), such as naproxen (Aleve) or ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin IB, others). These medications may relieve your pain soon after your

headache begins.

-Take triptans. Your doctor may prescribe triptans, medications that block pain signals in your brain. Triptans often may relieve pain from your headache within two hours and

help to control vomiting.
